  201→// deleteAlertRule stops evaluation of the rule, deletes it from active rules, and cleans up state cache.\n   202→func (sch *schedule) deleteAlertRule(ctx context.Context, keys ...ngmodels.AlertRuleKey) {\n   203→\tfor _, key := range keys {\n   204→\t\t// It can happen that the scheduler has deleted the alert rule before the\n   205→\t\t// Ruler API has called schedulePeriodic(ctx context.Context, t *ticker.T) error {\n   247→\tdispatcherGroup, ctx := errgroup.WithContext(ctx)\n   248→\tfor {\n   249→\t\tselect {\n   250→\t\tcase tick := <-t.C:\n 262→\t\t\t// waiting for all rule evaluation routines to stop\n   263→\t\t\twaitErr := dispatcherGroup.Wait()\n   264→\t\t\treturn waitErr\n   265→\t\t}\n   266→\t}\n   267→}\n   268→\n   269→type readyToRunItem struct {\n   270→\truleRoutine Rule\n   271→\tEvaluation\n   272→}\n   273→\n   274→// TODO refactor to accept a callback for tests that will be called with things that are returned currently, and return nothing.\n   275→// Returns a slice of rules that were scheduled for evaluation, map of stopped rules, and a slice of updated rules\n   276→func (sch *schedule) processTick(ctx evaluation routine, optionally with a previous item to log the trigger source.\n   426→func (sch *schedule) runJobFn(next readyToRunItem, prev ...readyToRunItem) func() {\n   427→\treturn func() {\n   428→\t\tif len(prev) > 0 {\n   429→\t\t\tsch.log.Debug(\"Rule evaluation triggered by previous rule\", append(next.rule.GetKey().LogContext(), \"previousRule\", prev[0].rule.UID)...)\n   430→\t\t}\n The scheduler's main entry point is the Run() method, which creates a ticker via ticker.New() (pkg/services/ngalert/schedule/ticker/ticker.go) that emits periodic ticks at regular intervals. The Run() method then calls schedulePeriodic() to enter the event loop. In schedulePeriodic(), the scheduler waits for ticks from the ticker and for each tick calls processTick() to determine which alert rules should be evaluated. The processTick() function builds a list of rules ready to run and uses buildSequences() to organize them, then calls runSequences() to execute them. The runJobFn() method at line 426-442 is where evaluation cycle overruns are detected.
